<p><b>Super League</b> (currently known as the <b>Betfred Super League</b> for sponsorship reasons) is the top-level professional <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> club competition in the Northern Hemisphere. The league has twelve teams: eleven from England and one from France.
</p><p>Super League began in 1996, replacing the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League_Championship_First_Division" title="Rugby Football League Championship First Division">Rugby Football League Championship</a> and switching from a winter to a summer season. Each team plays 29 games between February and September: 11 home games, 11 away games, <a href="/wiki/Magic_Weekend" title="Magic Weekend">Magic Weekend</a> and an additional 6 'loop fixtures' decided by league positions. The top five then enter the <a href="/wiki/Super_League_play-offs" title="Super League play-offs">play-off series</a> leading to the <a href="/wiki/Super_League_Grand_Final" title="Super League Grand Final">Grand Final</a> which determines the champions. The bottom team is relegated to the <a href="/wiki/RFL_Championship" title="RFL Championship">Championship</a>.
</p><p>The Super League champions play the <a href="/wiki/National_Rugby_League" title="National Rugby League">National Rugby League</a> champions from <a href="/wiki/Australasia" title="Australasia">Australasia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/World_Club_Challenge" title="World Club Challenge">World Club Challenge</a> at the start of the season.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="1996.E2.80.932001:_Establishment"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1996–2001:_Establishment">1996–2001: Establishment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1996–2001: Establishment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A "super league" competition was first mooted during the Australian <a href="/wiki/Super_League_war" title="Super League war">Super League war</a> as a way for <a href="/wiki/Rupert_Murdoch" title="Rupert Murdoch">Rupert Murdoch</a> to gain the upper hand during the battle for broadcasting supremacy with the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Rugby_League" title="Australian Rugby League">Australian Rugby League</a>. Murdoch also approached the British clubs to form Super League. A large sum of money aided the decision, and the competition got under way in 1996. Part of the deal saw rugby league switch from a winter to a summer season. The 12 founding teams of Super League were:
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 20em; -webkit-column-width: 20em; column-width: 20em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/File:Bullscolours.svg" class="image"><img alt="Bullscolours.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Bullscolours.svg/16px-Bullscolours.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Bullscolours.svg/24px-Bullscolours.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Bullscolours.svg/32px-Bullscolours.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="117" data-file-height="117" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Bulls" title="Bradford Bulls">Bradford Bulls</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:Castleford_colours.svg" class="image"><img alt="Castleford colours.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Castleford_colours.svg/16px-Castleford_colours.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Castleford_colours.svg/24px-Castleford_colours.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Castleford_colours.svg/32px-Castleford_colours.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="117" data-file-height="117" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Castleford_Tigers" title="Castleford Tigers">Castleford Tigers</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:Faxcolours.svg" class="image"><img alt="Faxcolours.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Faxcolours.svg/16px-Faxcolours.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Faxcolours.svg/24px-Faxcolours.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Faxcolours.svg/32px-Faxcolours.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="117" data-file-height="117" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Halifax_R.L.F.C." title="Halifax R.L.F.C.">Halifax</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:Rhinoscolours.svg" class="image"><img alt="Rhinoscolours.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Rhinoscolours.svg/16px-Rhinoscolours.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Rhinoscolours.svg/24px-Rhinoscolours.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Rhinoscolours.svg/32px-Rhinoscolours.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="117" data-file-height="117" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds Rhinos</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:Broncoscolours.png" class="image"><img alt="Broncoscolours.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Broncoscolours.png/16px-Broncoscolours.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Broncoscolours.png/24px-Broncoscolours.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Broncoscolours.png/32px-Broncoscolours.png 2x" data-file-width="118" data-file-height="118" /></a> <a href="/wiki/London_Broncos" title="London Broncos">London Broncos</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:Oldhamcolours.svg" class="image"><img alt="Oldhamcolours.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Oldhamcolours.svg/16px-Oldhamcolours.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Oldhamcolours.svg/24px-Oldhamcolours.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Oldhamcolours.svg/32px-Oldhamcolours.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="117" data-file-height="117" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Bears" class="mw-redirect" title="Oldham Bears">Oldham Bears</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:France_colours.svg" class="image"><img alt="France colours.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0b/France_colours.svg/16px-France_colours.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0b/France_colours.svg/24px-France_colours.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0b/France_colours.svg/32px-France_colours.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="117" data-file-height="117" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_Rugby_League" title="Paris Saint-Germain Rugby League">Paris Saint-Germain</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffeagles_colours.svg" class="image"><img alt="Sheffeagles colours.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Sheffeagles_colours.svg/16px-Sheffeagles_colours.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Sheffeagles_colours.svg/24px-Sheffeagles_colours.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Sheffeagles_colours.svg/32px-Sheffeagles_colours.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="117" data-file-height="117" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Eagles_(1984)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Eagles (1984)">Sheffield Eagles</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:Saintscolours.svg" class="image"><img alt="Saintscolours.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Saintscolours.svg/16px-Saintscolours.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Saintscolours.svg/24px-Saintscolours.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Saintscolours.svg/32px-Saintscolours.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="118" data-file-height="118" /></a> <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_R.F.C." title="St Helens R.F.C.">St. Helens</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:Wolvescolours.svg" class="image"><img alt="Wolvescolours.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Wolvescolours.svg/16px-Wolvescolours.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Wolvescolours.svg/24px-Wolvescolours.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Wolvescolours.svg/32px-Wolvescolours.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="118" data-file-height="118" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Warrington_Wolves" title="Warrington Wolves">Warrington Wolves</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:Wigancolours.svg" class="image"><img alt="Wigancolours.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Wigancolours.svg/16px-Wigancolours.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Wigancolours.svg/24px-Wigancolours.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Wigancolours.svg/32px-Wigancolours.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="117" data-file-height="117" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Warriors" title="Wigan Warriors">Wigan Warriors</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File:Workingtoncolours.svg" class="image"><img alt="Workingtoncolours.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Workingtoncolours.svg/16px-Workingtoncolours.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Workingtoncolours.svg/24px-Workingtoncolours.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Workingtoncolours.svg/32px-Workingtoncolours.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="118" data-file-height="118" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Workington_Town" title="Workington Town">Workington Town</a></li></ul>
</div>
<p>Initially, several mergers between existing clubs were proposed:
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 20em; -webkit-column-width: 20em; column-width: 20em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Castleford_Tigers" title="Castleford Tigers">Castleford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wakefield_Trinity" title="Wakefield Trinity">Wakefield Trinity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Featherstone_Rovers" title="Featherstone Rovers">Featherstone Rovers</a> would form Calder</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hull_F.C." title="Hull F.C.">Hull F.C.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hull_Kingston_Rovers" title="Hull Kingston Rovers">Hull Kingston Rovers</a> would form Hull</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Salford_Red_Devils" title="Salford Red Devils">Salford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oldham_R.L.F.C." title="Oldham R.L.F.C.">Oldham</a> were to form Manchester</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Eagles_(1984)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield Eagles (1984)">Sheffield Eagles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_R.L.F.C." title="Doncaster R.L.F.C.">Doncaster</a> were to form South Yorkshire</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Warrington_Wolves" title="Warrington Wolves">Warrington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Widnes_Vikings" title="Widnes Vikings">Widnes</a> were to form Cheshire</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Whitehaven_R.L.F.C." title="Whitehaven R.L.F.C.">Whitehaven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Workington_Town" title="Workington Town">Workington Town</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barrow_Raiders" title="Barrow Raiders">Barrow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carlisle_RLFC" title="Carlisle RLFC">Carlisle</a> would form Cumbria</li></ul>
</div>
<p>They were to be included with the following stand-alone clubs: <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Bulls" title="Bradford Bulls">Bradford Northern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Halifax_R.L.F.C." title="Halifax R.L.F.C.">Halifax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Broncos#1994–2005:_Broncos_and_Super_League" title="London Broncos">London Broncos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_Rugby_League" title="Paris Saint-Germain Rugby League">Paris Saint-Germain</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_R.F.C." title="St Helens R.F.C.">St. Helens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Warriors" title="Wigan Warriors">Wigan</a>.
</p><p>However this proved so unpopular that only existing clubs were selected for the competition. The clubs finishing below 10th in the existing top flight were excluded, which meant Featherstone Rovers, Hull, Wakefield Trinity and Widnes were left out, as were pioneering club <a href="/wiki/Keighley_Cougars" title="Keighley Cougars">Keighley</a> who had just won the Second Division Championship. <a href="/wiki/London_Broncos" title="London Broncos">London Broncos</a>, who had come fourth in the Second Division, were "fast-tracked" in on commercial grounds. A new team, <a href="/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_Rugby_League" title="Paris Saint-Germain Rugby League">Paris Saint-Germain</a>, was created to give a French dimension. Between 1998 and 2000 there was no relegation from Super League.
</p>
<h3><span id="2002.E2.80.932008:_Promotion_and_relegation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2002–2008:_Promotion_and_relegation">2002–2008: Promotion and relegation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2002–2008: Promotion and relegation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After two years Paris were dropped from the competition. <a href="/wiki/Promotion_and_relegation" title="Promotion and relegation">Promotion and relegation</a> between Super League and the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_National_Leagues" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby League National Leagues">Rugby League National Leagues</a> was re-introduced, and in 2002 the Super League Europe (SLE) governing body re-integrated fully into the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League" title="Rugby Football League">Rugby Football League</a> (RFL). In 2006, French side <a href="/wiki/Catalans_Dragons" title="Catalans Dragons">Catalans Dragons</a> (also known as UTC or Les Catalans) from <a href="/wiki/Perpignan" title="Perpignan">Perpignan</a> joined the league, becoming the second non-English team to compete. To facilitate this move, two clubs were relegated from Super League at the end of the 2005 season: Leigh who finished bottom of the league were replaced by the one club coming up from the National Leagues and Widnes who finished 11th (and would have stayed up any other year) were dropped for Les Catalans, thus the number of clubs in Super League remained at 12.
</p>
<h3><span id="2009.E2.80.932014:_Licensing"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2009–2014:_Licensing">2009–2014: Licensing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2009–2014: Licensing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Super_League_licensing" title="Super League licensing">Super League licensing</a></div>
<p>Super League licences were announced in May 2005 by the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League" title="Rugby Football League">RFL</a> as the new determinant of the Super League competition's participants from <a href="/wiki/Super_League_XIV" title="Super League XIV">2009</a> in place of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League_wooden_spoon_winners&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Super League wooden spoon winners (page does not exist)">promotion and relegation</a>. The licences were awarded after consideration of more factors than just the on-the-field performance of a club.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCa_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCa-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/Super_League_XII" title="Super League XII">2007</a> automatic promotion and relegation was suspended for Super League with new teams to be admitted on a licence basis with the term of the licence to start in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCa_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCa-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The RFL stated that clubs applying to compete in Super League would be assessed by criteria in four areas (stadium facilities, finance and business performance, commercial and marketing and playing strength, including junior production and development) with the final evaluations and decisions being taken by the RFL board of directors.<sup id="cite_ref-RFLa_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RFLa-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Successful applicants were licensed for three years of Super League competition and<sup id="cite_ref-BBCe_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCe-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> three-yearly reviews of Super League membership took place to ensure ambitious clubs lower down the leagues can still be successful.<sup id="cite_ref-RFLa_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RFLa-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Points attained by each club's application are translated into licence grades A, B or C. Clubs who achieved an A or B Licence would be automatically awarded a place in Super League, while those who achieved a C Licence underwent further scrutiny before the RFL decided who made the final cut.<sup id="cite_ref-Powers_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Powers-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>First licensing period</b>
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9311_Super_League_licences" title="2009–11 Super League licences">2009–11 Super League licences</a></div>
<p>In June 2008, the RFL confirmed that Super League would be expanded from 12 teams to 14 in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-Slater_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slater-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Skyb_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skyb-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and on 22 July 2008 the RFL confirmed the teams awarded licences.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCb_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCb-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The teams announced were the 12 existing Super League teams along with <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Championships" title="Rugby League Championships">National League 1</a> teams, <a href="/wiki/Crusaders_Rugby_League" title="Crusaders Rugby League">Celtic Crusaders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salford_Red_Devils" title="Salford Red Devils">Salford</a>. Celtic Crusaders becoming the first Welsh team to play in Super League and the only team to be awarded a licence who had never played in the Super League previously.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Featherstone_Rovers" title="Featherstone Rovers">Featherstone Rovers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Halifax_R.L.F.C." title="Halifax R.L.F.C.">Halifax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leigh_Centurions" title="Leigh Centurions">Leigh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Widnes_Vikings" title="Widnes Vikings">Widnes</a> all failed to attain a licence. Leigh and Widnes, especially, were disappointed with their exclusions with Leigh's chairman being extremely critical of the RFL.<sup id="cite_ref-Laybourn_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Laybourn-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Second licensing period</b>
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9314_Super_League_licences" title="2012–14 Super League licences">2012–14 Super League licences</a></div>
<p>For the 2012–14 seasons Championship sides <a href="/wiki/Batley_Bulldogs" title="Batley Bulldogs">Batley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barrow_Raiders" title="Barrow Raiders">Barrow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Featherstone_Rovers" title="Featherstone Rovers">Featherstone Rovers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Halifax_R.L.F.C." title="Halifax R.L.F.C.">Halifax</a> and <a href="/wiki/Widnes_Vikings" title="Widnes Vikings">Widnes</a> all met the on-field criteria needed to submit an application,<sup id="cite_ref-BBCh_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCh-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> but despite this only Barrow, Halifax and Widnes decided to submit an application.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCi_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCi-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> On 31 March 2011 <a href="/wiki/Widnes_Vikings" title="Widnes Vikings">Widnes</a> were awarded a Super League licence; <a href="/wiki/Barrow_Raiders" title="Barrow Raiders">Barrow</a>, did not meet the criteria and were refused a licence; and Halifax's application was to be further considered alongside the other Super League clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-Widnes_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Widnes-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League" title="Rugby Football League">Rugby Football League</a>'s final decision was announced on 26 July 2011, Widnes would be joining thirteen existing Super League teams with <a href="/wiki/Crusaders_Rugby_League" title="Crusaders Rugby League">Crusaders RL</a> having withdrawn their application and Halifax not meeting the criteria.<sup id="cite_ref-Licence_2012_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Licence_2012-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Crusaders CEO Rod Findlay stated that the club's finances were not in a good enough condition to justify their place in Super League.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCj_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCj-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Halifax chairman Mark Steele was critical of the decision to award Wakefield a licence over themselves, saying "If you compare Belle Vue with the Shay, it's no contest; if you compare playing records, it's no contest; and if you compare the financial position, we have kept our head above water and they haven't."<sup id="cite_ref-BBCj_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCj-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Wakefield had been favourites to lose their licence before Crusaders' withdrawal.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCj_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCj-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2015.E2.80.932018:_Super_8s"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015–2018:_Super_8s">2015–2018: Super 8s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2015–2018: Super 8s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Super_8s" title="Rugby League Super 8s">Rugby League Super 8s</a></div>
<p>At the 2013 Annual General Meeting at <a href="/wiki/Bradford" title="Bradford">Bradford</a>, the Super League clubs agreed to reduce the number of clubs to 12 from 2015, and also for a return of Promotion and Relegation with a 12 club <a href="/wiki/RFL_Championship" title="RFL Championship">Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 12 First Utility Super League and 12 <a href="/wiki/RFL_Championship" title="RFL Championship">Kingstone Press Championship</a> clubs will play each other home and away over 22 "rounds", plus a <a href="/wiki/Magic_Weekend" title="Magic Weekend">Magic Weekend</a> for both divisions, making a 23-game regular season. Following the conclusion of their regular league seasons, the 24 clubs will then compete in a play-off series where they split into 3 leagues of 8 based upon league position:<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>The top 8 Super League clubs will continue to compete in the <b><a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Super_8s" title="Rugby League Super 8s">Super 8s</a></b>. After playing each other once (either home or away), the top 4 clubs will progress to the semi-finals to determine who will compete in the <a href="/wiki/Super_League_Grand_Final" title="Super League Grand Final">Grand Final</a> and be crowned champions.</li>
<li>The remaining (bottom 4) Super League clubs and the top 4 Championship clubs will compete in <b><a href="/wiki/The_Qualifiers" title="The Qualifiers">The Qualifiers</a></b>. They will play each other once (either home or away) to determine which four of the clubs will compete in Super League the following year.</li></ul>
<p>Funding for clubs will be tiered in both leagues to prevent relegation related financial difficulties.
</p><p>In June 2015 8 of the 12 Super League clubs voted to allow a <b>Marquee Player</b> that can exceed a clubs salary cap as long as they can afford their wages. The marquee player rule came into force for the 2016 Super League season.
</p>
<h3><span id="2019.E2.80.93onwards:_One_up_one_down"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2019–onwards:_One_up_one_down">2019–onwards: One up one down</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2019–onwards: One up one down">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">September 2018</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>On 14 September 2018, an EGM was called to discuss the future of the sport and a change in structure, as the clubs were in favour of scrapping the Super 8s in favour of a more conventional structure. Two proposals were put forward: one by Super League and one by the Championship and League 1;
</p><p><b>Super League proposal:</b> The Super League proposed staying with 12 teams who play each other home and away plus Magic Weekend and 6 loop fixtures (29 games). They also proposed a return to a top-5 playoff and the 12th placed team being relegated.
</p><p><b>Championship &amp; League 1 proposal:</b> The alternative proposal was that Super League would expand to 14 clubs playing 27 games ending with a top-5 playoff. The team finishing 14th would be relegated and 13th would play 2nd, 3rd and 4th in the Championship in a relegation playoff.
</p><p>After a vote, the Super League proposal was voted through and is due to be implemented for the 2019 season.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Super_League_regular_season">Super League regular season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Super League regular season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>12 teams compete in Super League. They play each other twice on a home-and-away basis, interrupted by the <a href="/wiki/Magic_Weekend" title="Magic Weekend">Magic Weekend</a> round in May. The 12 clubs also play 6 loop fixtures to bring the number of games in a season to 29. The team finishing bottom after 29 rounds collects the Wooden Spoon, and is relegated, while the team finishing first is awarded the <a href="/wiki/League_Leaders_Shield" class="mw-redirect" title="League Leaders Shield">League Leaders Shield</a>. The top 5 teams at the end of the season enter the playoffs.
</p><p>Super League will be adopting <a href="/wiki/Golden_point" title="Golden point">Golden point</a> during regular season for the first time as of the start of the 2019 season, bringing it in line with the <a href="/wiki/National_Rugby_League" title="National Rugby League">NRL</a> which has been using the system since 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Magic_Weekend">Magic Weekend</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Magic Weekend">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Magic_Weekend" title="Magic Weekend">Magic Weekend</a></div>
<p>In an attempt to expand out of the traditional rugby league "heartlands", and market the game to a wider audience, the RFL has staged games in large stadia, in places without a strong rugby league presence. The "<a href="/wiki/Magic_Weekend" title="Magic Weekend">Magic Weekend</a>" concept, which involves staging an entire round of Super League in such a stadium, was first staged in <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a> in 2007. Dubbed "Millennium Magic", and played in the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a>, the concept was held in Cardiff again in 2008. In 2009 and 2010, the event was held in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> at the Scottish national rugby union stadium, giving rise to the name changing to "Murrayfield Magic". Generally held during the May Day weekend, 2011 saw the Magic Weekend return to Cardiff, and was held during the weekend 12–13 February, and serving as the season opener.  from 2014-2018, the event was held at <a href="/wiki/St_James%27_Park" title="St James&#39; Park">St James' Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle</a>.
In 2019, the event will be held at <a href="/wiki/Anfield" title="Anfield">Anfield</a> in <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Play-offs">Play-offs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Play-offs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Super_League_play-offs" title="Super League play-offs">Super League play-offs</a></div>
<p>The play-offs have had various formats. <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_RFC" class="mw-redirect" title="St Helens RFC">St Helens</a> are the only team to take part in every playoff series since the inaugural series in <a href="/wiki/Super_League_III" title="Super League III">1998</a>
</p><p>The current play-off system was previously used between 1998 and 2001. The same system was used in the <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales_Rugby_League" title="New South Wales Rugby League">NSWRL</a>'s Sydney Competition 1973-1994, the <a href="/wiki/Super_League_(Australia)" title="Super League (Australia)">Australian Super League</a> in its only season 1997, the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_League" title="Australian Football League">VFL</a>, 1972–1990 and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Rugby_League" title="New Zealand Rugby League">New Zealand's</a> <a href="/wiki/Lion_Red_Cup" title="Lion Red Cup">Lion Red Cup</a>, 1994–1996, and <a href="/wiki/Bartercard_Cup" title="Bartercard Cup">Bartercard Cup</a>, 2000-2006.
</p><p>From week two on the Top five play-offs system reflected exactly the <a href="/wiki/Page_playoff_system" title="Page playoff system">Page playoff system</a>.
</p><p><b>The Top Five Super League Play-Off Structure:</b>
</p><p><b>Week One</b>
</p>
<dl><dd><ul><li>Qualification Final: 2nd vs 3rd</li>
<li>Elimination Final: 4th vs 5th</li>
<li>Bye: 1</li></ul></dd></dl>
<p><b>Week Two</b>
</p>
<dl><dd><ul><li>Major Semi Final: 1st vs Winners of Qualification Final</li>
<li>Minor Semi Final: Losers of Qualification Final vs Winners of Elimination Final</li></ul></dd></dl>
<p><b>Week Three</b>
</p>
<dl><dd><ul><li>Preliminary Final: Losers of Major Semi Final vs Winners of Minor Semi Final</li>
<li>Bye: Winners of Major Semi Final</li></ul></dd></dl>
<p><b>Week Four</b>
</p>
<dl><dd><ul><li>Grand Final: Winners of Major Semi Final vs Winners of Preliminary Final</li></ul></dd></dl>
<center>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grand_Final">Grand Final</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Grand Final">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Super_League_Grand_Final" title="Super League Grand Final">Super League Grand Final</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rhinos2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Rhinos2008.jpg/220px-Rhinos2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Rhinos2008.jpg/330px-Rhinos2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Rhinos2008.jpg/440px-Rhinos2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rhinos2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds Rhinos</a> celebrating following their <a href="/wiki/2008_Super_League_Grand_Final" title="2008 Super League Grand Final">2008 Grand Final</a> victory</div></div></div>
<p>The Grand Final is the championship-deciding game and showpiece event of the Super League season. It is held annually at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a>.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_competitions">Other competitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Other competitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Challenge_Cup">Challenge Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Challenge Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Challenge_Cup" title="Challenge Cup">Challenge Cup</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Challenge_Cup" title="Challenge Cup">Challenge Cup</a> is a separate cup competition, involving clubs from Super League and all levels of rugby league in Britain. It has been held annually since 1896 and has been expanded so teams in Russia, France, Scotland and Wales can take part. The cup runs throughout the season, and the final is usually played on the August bank holiday at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>. Until Super League, the final would take place at Wembley Stadium at the end of April or start of May, usually 2 weeks after the regular season ended.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academies">Academies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Academies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Reserve_league">Reserve league</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Reserve league">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/RFL_Reserve_Championship" title="RFL Reserve Championship">RFL Reserve Championship</a></div>
<p>In 2014 and 2015 Super League clubs were unhappy with the Dual registration system and wanted to form an under-23 reserve leagues between the under-19s and first teams. Wigan, Warrington and St Helens were the first teams to propose the return of the reserve league where players could move from the under 19s and play with professional players before playing in the first team. A reserve league was set up in 2016 with a mixture of Super League, Championship and League 1 teams.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dual_registration">Dual registration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Dual registration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Dual_registration" title="Rugby League Dual registration">Rugby League Dual registration</a></div>
<p>Dual registration refers to an arrangement between clubs whereby a player continues to be registered to his current Super League club and is also registered to play for a club in the Championship. The system is aimed at young Super League players who are thought to be not quite ready to make the step up to 'week in, week out' Super League first team duties but for whom first team match experience is likely to be beneficial for their development.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Only Super League players can be dual registered and the receiving club must be a club in the Championships, meaning that Super League to Super League club dual registrations are not available.</li>
<li>A dual registered player will be eligible to play and train with both clubs in a format agreed between the clubs, subject to registration, salary cap and competition eligibility rules.</li>
<li>The player is restricted to playing in one fixture per scheduled round of fixtures in any given week and would not be eligible to play for his Super League club on a Thursday and in a Championship fixture at the weekend, for example.</li>
<li>A receiving club will be limited to a total of five dual registered players per matchday squad.</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Under_19s">Under 19s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Under 19s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Super_League_Under_19s" title="Super League Under 19s">Super League Under 19s</a></div>

<b>Super League Academy – U19s</b>:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r891159353">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .multicol-float{width:auto!important}}.mw-parser-output .multicol-float{width:30em}</style><div class="multicol-float" style="clear:none;float:left;">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Champions">Champions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Champions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl><dd><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Super_League_seasons" title="List of Super League seasons">List of Super League seasons</a></div></dd>
<dd><i>See <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League_Championship_First_Division" title="Rugby Football League Championship First Division">Rugby Football League Championship</a> for the all-time list of champions since 1895.</i></dd></dl>
<p>The league format changed in 1998 and the championship became a play-off series to determine the Super League champions. This meant a reintroduction of a final to determine the European champions, the first since the <a href="/wiki/1972%E2%80%9373_Northern_Rugby_Football_League_season" title="1972–73 Northern Rugby Football League season">1972–73 season</a>. For the first 2 seasons of Super League, there was no Grand Final - The winners of the league were the team that finished top, as before in the previous Championship leagues.
</p>

<tr style="background:#f5faff;">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Double">The Double</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: The Double">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Double_(rugby_league)" title="The Double (rugby league)">The Double (rugby league)</a></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a>, the term 'the Double' is referring to the achievement of a club that wins the top division and Challenge Cup in the same season. To date, this has been achieved by a total ten different clubs but by only four different clubs during the Super League era.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Treble">The Treble</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: The Treble">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Treble_(rugby_league)" title="The Treble (rugby league)">The Treble (rugby league)</a></div>
<p>The <i>Treble</i> refers to the team who wins all three domestic honours on offer during the season; Grand Final, <a href="/wiki/League_Leaders%27_Shield" title="League Leaders&#39; Shield">League Leaders' Shield</a> and Challenge Cup. To date seven teams have won the treble, only <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Bulls" title="Bradford Bulls">Bradford Bulls</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_R.F.C." title="St Helens R.F.C.">St. Helens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds Rhinos</a> have won the treble in the Super League era.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="All_Four_Cups">All Four Cups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: All Four Cups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/All_Four_Cups" title="All Four Cups">All Four Cups</a></div>
<p>Winning all <b>Four Cups</b> refers to winning the <a href="/wiki/Super_League_Grand_Final" title="Super League Grand Final">Super League</a>, <a href="/wiki/League_Leaders%27_Shield" title="League Leaders&#39; Shield">League Leaders' Shield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Challenge_Cup" title="Challenge Cup">Challenge Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Club_Challenge" title="World Club Challenge">World Club Challenge</a> in one season. Not all of these cups were available in the past but have replaced other cups that could be won.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="League_Leaders.27_Shield"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="League_Leaders'_Shield">League Leaders' Shield</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: League Leaders&#039; Shield">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/League_Leaders%27_Shield" title="League Leaders&#39; Shield">League Leaders' Shield</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/League_Leaders%27_Shield" title="League Leaders&#39; Shield">League Leaders' Shield</a> is awarded to the team finishing the regular season top of Super League; this is also known as a <a href="/wiki/Minor_premiership" title="Minor premiership">minor premiership</a>. The League Leader's Shield was introduced only in 2003, previously no prize was awarded to the team finishing top following the introduction of the Grand Final.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Super_League_Trophy">Super League Trophy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Super League Trophy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2012SuperLeagueTrophy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/da/2012SuperLeagueTrophy.jpg/150px-2012SuperLeagueTrophy.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/da/2012SuperLeagueTrophy.jpg/225px-2012SuperLeagueTrophy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/d/da/2012SuperLeagueTrophy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="243" data-file-height="408" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2012SuperLeagueTrophy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Super League Trophy</div></div></div>
<p>The winner of the Grand Final is given the Super League Trophy as Super League Champions. This is considered more prestigious than the minor premiership. Each year, the year of a champion team's triumph, team name and team Rugby league football <a href="/wiki/Captain_(sports)" title="Captain (sports)">captain</a> are engraved.
</p><p>The record for most Super League titles won is held by <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds</a> with eight titles. <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds</a> captain <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Sinfield" title="Kevin Sinfield">Kevin Sinfield</a> currently holds the record for captaining the most Super League title winning sides after captaining Leeds to their first 7 grand final successes. <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_R.F.C." title="St Helens R.F.C.">St. Helens</a> contested the final 6 years in a row (from 2006 until 2011) during which time they succeeded only once in lifting the trophy against <a href="/wiki/Hull_F.C." title="Hull F.C.">Hull F.C.</a> in 2006; after which they suffered consecutive defeats against <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds</a> in 2007, 2008, 2009, <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Warriors" title="Wigan Warriors">Wigan</a> in 2010 and <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds</a> once again in 2011. However, <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_R.F.C." title="St Helens R.F.C.">St. Helens</a> made a victorious return in 2014, defeating rivals, <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Warriors" title="Wigan Warriors">Wigan</a> 14–6.
</p><p>Following their 2014 and 2015 defeats to <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_R.F.C." title="St Helens R.F.C.">St. Helens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds</a> respectively, <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Warriors" title="Wigan Warriors">Wigan</a> have now equalled <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_R.F.C." title="St Helens R.F.C.">St Helens's</a> record of losing five Grand Finals. Hull FC (2006), Warrington (2012, 2013, 2016, and 2018), and <a href="/wiki/Castleford_Tigers" title="Castleford Tigers">Castleford</a> (2017) have all appeared in the Grand Final but never won.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Steve_Prescott_Man_of_Steel_award">Steve Prescott Man of Steel award</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Steve Prescott Man of Steel award">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Man_of_Steel_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Man of Steel Award">Man of Steel Award</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Man_of_Steel_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Man of Steel Award">Man of Steel Award</a> is an annual award for the best player of the season in Super League. It has continued from pre-Super League times, with the first such award given in 1977. It was renamed in honour of <a href="/wiki/Steve_Prescott" title="Steve Prescott">Steve Prescott</a> in 2014.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Albert_Goldthorpe_Medal">Albert Goldthorpe Medal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Albert Goldthorpe Medal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Albert_Goldthorpe_Medal" title="Albert Goldthorpe Medal">Albert Goldthorpe Medal</a></div>
<p>The <b>Albert Goldthorpe Medal</b> is an award voted for be members of the press who cast a vote after every game of the regular season. The three players who, in the opinion of the reporter, have been the three 'best and fairest' players in the game will receive three points, two points and one point respectively. To be eligible for a vote, a player must not have been suspended from the competition at any stage during the season.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Super_League_Dream_Team">Super League Dream Team</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Super League Dream Team">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Head_coaches_with_Super_League_titles">Head coaches with Super League titles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Head coaches with Super League titles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Super League has been won by 13 different coaches, 8 from Australia, 4 from England and 1 from New Zealand.

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Players_to_have_made_over_350_Super_League_Appearances">Players to have made over 350 Super League Appearances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Players to have made over 350 Super League Appearances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Logo">Logo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Logo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:128px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Super_League_logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/52/Super_League_logo.png" decoding="async" width="126" height="149" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="126" data-file-height="149" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Super_League_logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Super League logo until 2016</div></div></div>
<p>The Super League has had two official logos. The first was used for the inaugural season in 1996 and until 2016. The logo had the Super League <b>S</b> with Super above it and League below it. The title sponsors name would appear above the logo until 2014 when title sponsors <a href="/wiki/First_Utility" class="mw-redirect" title="First Utility">First Utility</a> used their own personalised logos that appeared on player shirts and in the media. The reigning champions had a ribbon around the logo with champions on it until 2011.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Super_League_logo_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a5/Super_League_logo_2017.jpg/220px-Super_League_logo_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="99" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a5/Super_League_logo_2017.jpg/330px-Super_League_logo_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a5/Super_League_logo_2017.jpg/440px-Super_League_logo_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="469" data-file-height="212" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Super_League_logo_2017.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2017 rebrand</div></div></div>
<p>The second official logo was introduced in 2017 as part of a radical rebrand across British rugby league. The design was similar to the <a href="/wiki/RFL" class="mw-redirect" title="RFL">RFL</a> and <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_league_team" title="England national rugby league team">England</a> logos. It had a rectangular backdrop representing the George Hotel, where rugby league was founded, thirteen lines representing thirteen players, a chevron which are well known for appearing on rugby league shirts and the <b>S</b> which represents the ball and the Super League. The current champions have a gold logo.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Sponsorship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Betfred_Super_League_logo.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/90/Betfred_Super_League_logo.jpeg/220px-Betfred_Super_League_logo.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/90/Betfred_Super_League_logo.jpeg/330px-Betfred_Super_League_logo.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/90/Betfred_Super_League_logo.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="388" data-file-height="257" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Betfred_Super_League_logo.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sponsorship logo used in media and on players shirts</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/English_rugby_league_sponsorship" title="English rugby league sponsorship">English rugby league sponsorship</a></div>
<p>Super League has been sponsored since its formation, apart from the 2013 season.
</p><p>The title sponsor has been able to determine the league's sponsorship name. There have been seven different title sponsors since the league's formation:
</p>

<p>As well as title sponsorship, Super League has a number of official partners and suppliers.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> For the 2017 season these include <a href="/wiki/Kingstone_Press_Cider" title="Kingstone Press Cider">Kingstone Press Cider</a>, <a href="/wiki/Automobile_Dacia" title="Automobile Dacia">Dacia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bwin.Party_Digital_Entertainment#Bingo" title="Bwin.Party Digital Entertainment">Foxy Bingo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Batchelors" title="Batchelors">Batchelors</a> and <a href="/wiki/Specsavers" title="Specsavers">Specsavers</a>.
</p><p>The official <a href="/wiki/Rugby_ball" title="Rugby ball">rugby ball</a> supplier is <a href="/wiki/Steeden" title="Steeden">Steeden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition_rules">Competition rules</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Competition rules">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overseas_quota_and_Federation-trained_players">Overseas quota and Federation-trained players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Overseas quota and Federation-trained players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An overseas quota restricting the maximum number of foreign players at each club has existed since the inception of the Super League in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> However, overseas players that hold a <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> passport or come under the <a href="/wiki/Kolpak_ruling" title="Kolpak ruling">Kolpak ruling</a> do not count towards the quota. This resulted in the number of non-British players at some clubs greatly exceeding the quota.
</p><p>In response to concerns over the growing number of foreign players in the league, in 2007, the RFL announced plans to introduce a "homegrown player" rule to encourage clubs to develop their own players.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> As of 2017, Super League clubs are permitted to register no more than five overseas players. Additionally, squads are also limited to a maximum of seven non-Federation trained players.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Salary_cap">Salary cap</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Salary cap">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A salary cap was first introduced to the Super League in 1998, with clubs being allowed to spend up to 50 percent of their income on player wages. From the 2002 season onwards, the cap became a fixed ceiling of £1.8 million in order to increase parity within the league.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Super League operates under a real-time salary cap system that will calculate a club's salary cap position at the start of and throughout the season:<sup id="cite_ref-5nSmnqm00_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5nSmnqm00-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>The combined earnings of the top 25 players must not exceed £1.825 million.</li>
<li>Clubs will only be allowed to sign a new player if they have room under the cap.</li>
<li>Clubs are allowed to spend a maximum of £50,000 on players outside the top 25 earners who have made at least one first grade appearance for the club during the year.</li>
<li>Costs for players outside of the top 25 earners who do not make a first team appearance will be unregulated.</li>
<li>Any player who has played for the same club for at least 10 consecutive seasons will have half their salary excluded from the salary cap for his 11th and subsequent seasons. This is subject to a maximum of £50,000 for any one club.</li>
<li>Clubs are allowed one "Marquee Player" who can exceed a club's salary cap as long as they can afford the players wages.</li></ul>
<p>In 2017, Super League clubs approved proposals to increase the salary cap over the next three seasons, eventually rising to £2.1 million by 2020. Clubs will also be allowed to sign a second marquee player.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Squad_announcement_system">Squad announcement system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Squad announcement system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Before each Super League and <a href="/wiki/Challenge_Cup" title="Challenge Cup">Tetley's Challenge Cup</a> fixture, each club must announce the squad of 19 players it will choose from by 2.00pm on the second day before the match day.<sup id="cite_ref-5nSmnqm00_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5nSmnqm00-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Match_officials">Match officials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Match officials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/RFL_Match_officials" class="mw-redirect" title="RFL Match officials">RFL Match officials</a></div>
<p>All Super League matches are governed by the laws set out by the RFL; these laws are enforced by match officials. Former Super League and International Referee <a href="/wiki/Steve_Ganson" title="Steve Ganson">Steve Ganson</a> is the current Head of Match Officials and Technical Director. Former <a href="/wiki/Hull_F.C." title="Hull F.C.">Hull F.C.</a> player and <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Giants" title="Huddersfield Giants">Huddersfield</a> Head Coach <a href="/wiki/Jon_Sharp" title="Jon Sharp">Jon Sharp</a> was the previous Head of Match Officials. Sharp was sacked in July 2015 and took up the role of Head Coach at Featherstone Rovers. He assumed his role at the RFL following <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Cummings" title="Stuart Cummings">Stuart Cummings</a>' departure in March 2013 having previously held the role of Match Officials Coach &amp; Technical Director.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>Since its formation in 1996 only four teams have won the Super League (<a href="/wiki/Bradford_Bulls" title="Bradford Bulls">Bradford Bulls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds Rhinos</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_R.F.C." title="St Helens R.F.C.">St. Helens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Warriors" title="Wigan Warriors">Wigan Warriors</a>). Also, only a total of seven teams have taken part in the <a href="/wiki/Super_League_Grand_Final" title="Super League Grand Final">Grand Final</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hull_F.C." title="Hull F.C.">Hull FC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castleford" title="Castleford">Castleford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warrington_Wolves" title="Warrington Wolves">Warrington Wolves</a> being the other three).  Seven different teams have been the league leaders, however only one of these (<a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Giants" title="Huddersfield Giants">Huddersfield Giants</a> in 2013) is a different team to those that have appeared in the grand final, meaning that only eight different teams have been involved in the grand final or topped the regular season table, however, a total of 23 teams have taken part in Super League since its inception.
</p><p>In comparison, in the same 22-year period, 12 different teams have won the Australasian <a href="/wiki/National_Rugby_League" title="National Rugby League">National Rugby League</a> competition and 15 different teams have appeared in the <a href="/wiki/NRL_Grand_Final" title="NRL Grand Final">Grand Final</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Licensing">Licensing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Licensing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Between 2009 and 2014 teams had to apply for a licence to play in Super League, this also meant there was no automatic promotion between Super League and the Championship. This was unpopular with Championship clubs because there was no fair and easy way for them to get promoted into Super League and it was seen as a closed shop.
</p><p>Attendances in the lower divisions dropped as a result of this system because it was felt that there was little appeal in these leagues when there was no incentive for the clubs to win the <a href="/wiki/RFL_Championship" title="RFL Championship">Championship</a>. Also the only time that lower division clubs got the chance to play Super League opposition was in the early rounds of the <a href="/wiki/Challenge_Cup" title="Challenge Cup">Challenge Cup</a>. With no route to the Super League however, teams were unable to compete with top division opposition because there was no way that clubs could attract top talent when players would not be playing in top-level rugby league.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="M62_Corridor">M62 Corridor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: M62 Corridor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league_in_Yorkshire" title="Rugby league in Yorkshire">Rugby league in Yorkshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league_in_Lancashire" title="Rugby league in Lancashire">Rugby league in Lancashire</a></div>
<p>Another Criticism of the Super League is that most of the teams that have competed in it have been in its heartlands of the M62 Corridor between Yorkshire and Lancashire. <a href="/wiki/Catalans_Dragons" title="Catalans Dragons">Catalans Dragons</a> and the <a href="/wiki/London_Broncos" title="London Broncos">London Broncos</a> are the only teams currently playing in Super League who are outside its traditional headland in the North of England, and are considered a success compared to teams such as the <a href="/wiki/North_Wales_Crusaders" title="North Wales Crusaders">North Wales Crusaders</a>.
</p><p>Expansion was a key policy of the <a href="/wiki/RFL" class="mw-redirect" title="RFL">RFL</a> when Super League was created.  Along with the above-mentioned teams, <a href="/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_Rugby_League" title="Paris Saint-Germain Rugby League">Paris Saint-Germain RL</a> competed from the beginning of the competition but departed after just two seasons due to a lack of interest and investment.  Another team to fail from outside the heartlands was <a href="/wiki/Gateshead_Thunder_(1999)" title="Gateshead Thunder (1999)">Gateshead Thunder</a> who competed in the first season of Super League.  After that first season they found themselves with debts of £700,000 and so accepted a grant of £1,250,000 to merge with <a href="/wiki/Hull_F.C." title="Hull F.C.">Hull FC</a>.
</p><p>Expansion has taken place in the lower divisions and this is a continuing policy of the <a href="/wiki/RFL" class="mw-redirect" title="RFL">RFL</a>.  At present nine expansion clubs take part in the lower divisions with 1 in the <a href="/wiki/RFL_Championship" title="RFL Championship">Championship</a> and 8 in the <a href="/wiki/League_1_(rugby_league)" title="League 1 (rugby league)">Championship 1</a>.  In 2015, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Toulouse_Olympique" title="Toulouse Olympique">Toulouse Olympique</a> had been granted entry into League 1, the third division of European rugby league; the team has previously competed in the Championship.  This brought the total number of expansion teams across the top 3 divisions to 10 (out of 39 clubs).  In 2016 it was announced that a team based in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> had also been granted access to League 1. <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Wolfpack" title="Toronto Wolfpack">Toronto Wolfpack</a> began to play in the 2017 season and take the number of expansion clubs to 11 (out of 40 clubs).  This also means that teams taking part in the top 3 divisions come from 4 countries and 2 continents.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_coverage">Media coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Media coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sky_Sports" title="Sky Sports">Sky Sports</a> have been the primary broadcast partner of Super League since its inaugural season in 1996. The current deal lasts until 2021 and covers 80 matches per season, rising to 100 from 2015. They currently have the rights to show live Super League games in both <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>; two live matches are broadcast each week – one on Thursday nights at 7:30pm (kick off 8pm) and another at 7:30pm on Friday nights (kick off 8pm). From 2014, they also simulcast all of <a href="/wiki/Catalans_Dragons" title="Catalans Dragons">Catalans Dragons</a>' home games and from 2015, will broadcast regular <a href="/wiki/RFL_Championship" title="RFL Championship">Kingstone Press Championship</a> matches.
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>
<th>Duration
</th>
<th>Broadcaster
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>1996–2021
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Sky_Sports" title="Sky Sports">Sky Sports</a>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Detailed Sky coverage</b>
</p>
<ul><li><b>Super League Thursday</b> starts at 7:30&#160;pm and consists of a preview of the weekends Super League fixtures before the first game of the weekend.</li>
<li><b>Super League Friday</b> includes one game with coverage starting at 7:30pm building up to the game.</li>
<li><b>Super League Saturday</b> usually shows <a href="/wiki/Catalans_Dragons" title="Catalans Dragons">Catalans Dragons</a> games kicking off at 5:00pm with coverage starting from 4:55pm. When the Super 8s begin other teams are shown with coverage starting at 2:30pm for games kicking off at 5:00pm.</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Highlights">Highlights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Highlights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In addition to Sky Sports' live coverage, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Sport" title="BBC Sport">BBC Sport</a> broadcast a weekly highlights programme called the <a href="/wiki/Super_League_Show" title="Super League Show">Super League Show</a>, usually presented by Tanya Arnold. This is broadcast to the <a href="/wiki/BBC_North_West" title="BBC North West">North West</a>, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Yorkshire" title="BBC Yorkshire">Yorkshire &amp; North Midlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/BBC_North_East_and_Cumbria" title="BBC North East and Cumbria">North East &amp; Cumbria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Yorkshire_and_Lincolnshire" title="BBC Yorkshire and Lincolnshire">East Yorkshire &amp; Lincolnshire</a> regions on BBC 1 on Monday nights (after 11pm) and is repeated nationally on BBC 2 on Tuesday afternoons.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> A national repeat was first broadcast overnight during the week since February 2008 when the then BBC Director of Sport, Roger Mosey, commented that this move was in response to the growing popularity and awareness of the sport, and the large number of requests from people who want to watch it elsewhere in the UK. The end of season <a href="/wiki/Super_League_play-offs" title="Super League play-offs">play-off series</a> is shown nationwide in a highlights package. The Super League Show is also available for streaming or download using the <a href="/wiki/BBC_iPlayer" title="BBC iPlayer">BBC iPlayer</a> in the UK.
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Magazines">Magazines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Magazines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Regular commentator is <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Hemmings_(rugby_league)" title="Eddie Hemmings (rugby league)">Eddie Hemmings</a> and formerly <a href="/wiki/Mike_Stephenson" title="Mike Stephenson">Mike Stephenson</a> with summarisers including <a href="/wiki/Phil_Clarke" title="Phil Clarke">Phil Clarke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Carney_(rugby)" title="Brian Carney (rugby)">Brian Carney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barrie_McDermott" title="Barrie McDermott">Barrie McDermott</a> and <a href="/wiki/Terry_O%27Connor_(rugby_league)" title="Terry O&#39;Connor (rugby league)">Terry O'Connor</a>. Live Super League broadcasts regularly rank amongst the top 10 most watched programmes in a week on Sky Sports with in excess of 250,000 viewers.<sup id="cite_ref-Triline_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Triline-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Sky Sports also run several supplementary magazine shows, including Super League Full Time and <i><a href="/wiki/Boots_N%27_All" class="mw-redirect" title="Boots N&#39; All">Boots N' All</a></i>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Premier_Sports" title="Premier Sports">Premier Sports</a> and <a href="/wiki/Made_in_Leeds" class="mw-redirect" title="Made in Leeds">Made in Leeds</a> show a rugby league magazine program called <b>Rugby AM</b> hosted by Alex Simmons, <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Jones_Buchanan" class="mw-redirect" title="Jamie Jones Buchanan">Jamie Jones Buchanan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Keith_Senior" title="Keith Senior">Keith Senior</a>. It is aired on a Thursday night at 7 and is also repeated on Saturday. Rugby AM also has a radio show on All Star FM.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="International">International</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_League&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: International">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
